<Author>GD2004
<Content>Really, really happy with the Circle Yeah, yeah you've heard it before - spectacular view, great and friendly staff, small room, reasonably priced. My kids and I had a fantastic time. We got a 14th floor partial ocean view which meant you turned the chairs to the right and wow. We were there five nights and I could've stayed ten, honestly.We liked the room. Small but comfortable. I've stayed before at outrigger reef and that was small, too, and not nearly as comfortable and we looked out at a wall. I did not miss the pool - two minutes and you are across at the beach, sand may not be as fine as in front of the Royal Hawiaian (so walk up the beach five minutes if you want) but you can rent chairs/umbrella/surfboard reasonably right there, catamaran, right there, park really clean and nightly free hula/music shows, right there.While it probably doesn't belong in a hotel review, I don't know where else to put it, so I will say a few other things about Waikiki and Oahu in general, because this site has been SO good to me (helped me plan trip to Utah this summer, Grand Canyon, Vegas, and now Honolulu) I want to pass some of the marvelous information along.Some general advice:That free hula/music show at Prince Kuhio park is great, free, and kids can play in water at sunset - what could be better? Tiki's is a really fun restaurant with great drinks and reasonable for waikiki prices. If you are going to Dukes near sunset hang out on the lower lanai, they will eventually put tables/chairs out there too and then you will have one with a much shorter wait than when upper lanai becomes available, and a table right on the sand. Food:While I liked the Royal Hawaiian's Luau much much better than the icky food/long drive to Paradise Cove, they DO NOT show you the pig. it is already prepared and in a chafing dish. While fun, am not sure that this is worth the high admission ticket. What IS worht it is the Royal H's brunch, make your own smoothies and omelettes, and a fabulous view plus Hawaiian music performed strolling past your table. Keo's Thai is very disappointing. Arty Thai, not fun Thai (i/e unsweet pad thai really isn't that fun), weak drinks. pretty room though, but I'll take the less sophisticated, much more enjoyable (great live contemporary music!) Tiki's any time.Good bar eats and the best drinks at Sheraton Moana, and more music, this fairly traditional. great sunset view of diamond head.DO check out Waimanolo beach, maybe an hour outside of Waikiki. gorgeous and deserted and nice for swimming. And in the same town go to Keneke's. Do not be put off by the handpainted signs or slightly run down look. GREAT food, really inexpensive, really friendly.Climb Diamond Head but early, before it gets too hot (i.e. before 8 am) Check out Makupu point lighthouse, you do have to hike in now.Must have Matsumoto's ices in Haleiwa on N. Shore. With the beans!Ilioni palace was fun and worth touring, beware the one way streets.Chinatown is also alot of fun, I liked shopping in the afternoon, the lei store is fabulous - all sorts of exotics for $2, plus my daughter bought a chicken head for a quarter (not at the lei store) and got to terrorize her brother for hours of fun. If you get a surfing lesson from Palekaiko brothers at Kuhio Beach in waikiki ask for Roger. BEWARES:SKIP Hanama Bay, IMO. crowded, not many fish, the tedium of the 'don't feed fish, dont pee in the water' etc. lecture, the rude parking lot attendants - really not worth it. So many nicer snorkling spots toward the north shore and windward oahu. Do not want to draw too many to one specific spot but there are so many beautiful places. Just rent a car and drive along the coast route toward the N. Shore, and then return the fast way on the 99. We got to swim with a sea turtle and see dozens and dozens of beautiful fish - NOT in hanama.SKIP the L and L diner chain at least in Wahiawa, grease central, really really bad plate lunch, the complete opposite of Kenekes (our L and L went in the trash, literally).SKIP Waimea Bay Audobon Park falls - the falls are contaminated with bacteria. You CANNOT swim there (well you can if you ignore the life guard's warnings and don't mind murky water). the gardens are pretty but not as pretty as some around Honlulu and shouldn't you be out scoping the locals snorkling spots and windswept beaches instead?Aloha.  
<Date>Apr 22, 2005

<Author>Mme_X
<Content>Good value on Waikiki Admittedly, I've bumped this rating up a bit because of the mid-Century charm of the place, but there are drawbacks. The rooms are small, largely due to the goofy-fun nature of staying in a round building. The housekeeping was spotless. The partial ocean view was a delight (ours was not a direct ocean-front, but having coffee and hanging out on the balcony gave us an enjoyable beach view from the 7th floor.) Waikiki Beach is right across the street, and other restaurants, attractions (e.g. Surfrider's outdoor cocktail bar,) and shopping are an easy walk. I love the mid-century decorative touches, e.g. ocean motifs in the hall flooring. For the location and general pleasantness of the place, it's difficult to match the location at this price unless you get an unbelievable discount on one of the online travel sites.What you have to deal with: there is only one size room (small.) Since there seems to be only one size of bed (queen,) if you can't deal with two sleeping in one queen bed (we don't), then there are two queen beds in a small room that really squeezes the space. One king might have been better, but that doesn't seem to be an option. There was no real chest of drawers in our room, which made it difficult to work out of 2 large suitcases (we were traveling beyond Hawaii for a few weeks.) There is only a shower in the small bathroom. There is a desk in the closet and dressing, which could have held a suitcases, but we wanted that space for other needs. Finally, some types of maintenance could be a problem after hours. When we complained that our room safe (extra charge) did not have a key lock in it, we were told that it would be fixed the next day. NOT ACCEPTABLE, since in the interim we'd go out to dinner, go to the beach, etc. They finally called the hotel manager to do the repair since the maintenance man already left for the day. With all the Aston hotels in Waikiki, they couldn't have sent over one of the maintenance persons from another sister hotel? Otherwise, the service was very friendly and accomodating.To be honest, I'd stay again as a good value place with a fair amount of charm. My husband thought the place was fine enough, but would prefer to spend somewhat more to stay at the Marrriott, or other places we've stayed in Waikiki. The operative word is somewhat more: during holiday time, few Waikiki hotels are offering bargains.  
<Date>Jan 13, 2005

<Content>Loved, Loved and Loved the Wonderful Waikiki Circle Hotel I can't say enough good about this hotel. We stayed at this hotel for 1 week Dec 8-15. We had a wonderful stay. Rooms are rather small but there were three of us in this room and we also had 3 big suitcases and didnt have a problem with space. Besides, $146 for a Oceanfront room is a real value. The view was awsome. Bathrooms dont have bathtubs just showers(and no......they are not that small). The rooms are very clean, bright and cheery and have very large balconies. The room had a small refrigerator and the A/C always worked great. The lobby had lots of big fluffy beach towels you could use. Staff were always friendly. helpful and always had a smile. Free coffee bar and newspaper in the morning was wonderful. Maid service great. Nice fast elevators........never a wait. We went to the free hula show across the street every night. Only thing I disagree with at this hotel is this.....Hotel is a circle. Only the center rooms should be classified as Oceanfront. The other row of rooms on each side of the center rooms are also classified as oceanfront however they should not be as they are side oceanview in my opinion and not oceanfront. I received a side Oceanfront room and was disappointed, However, I asked the front desk for a Oceanfront center room and they switched me in two days. I would not hesitate to stay at this hotel again. Loved it!!!!!!!!!!

<Author>rainlvr
<Content>Worth it for the location and views I have to admit I was a little surprised at how small the rooms were when we walked in. There was still, however, plenty of room to put our stuff and a nice little side area with a good sized closet, desk, and refrigerator. Now even though I was surprised at the room size when I walked in, I was shocked when I checked out the bathroom! I really have never in my life seen such a miniature shower!! When I shampooed my hair I kept accidently bumping the faucet handle that controls the temperature and changing it. The water pressure is also really really low. I do think it's just a minor annoyance (and it's something I got used to pretty quickly - I mean, how long do you really spend in the shower anyways - just soap up, rinse off and get out!) What really made this hotel great was the cleanliness of the rooms (the carpet was spotless and looked brand new, the bedspreads looked freshly cleaned and the beds were very comfortable). Also, our ocean view room for $125/night was just beautiful - it was so nice to step outside and enjoy the view in the morning and evening!! My suggestion would be to just accept the itty bitty shower and small room size and just enjoy the views, location and a good nights sleep!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Location - Tiny Room I think everybody who has stayed in an ocean front room here would agree that the veiws are unbeatable. Unfortunately, the rooms are quite small (smaller than they appeared on the Aston website), and if you're over six feet tall you'll be painfully disproportionate to the small double beds. On the other hand, when our toilet started leaking water at the base all over the floor, it was fixed as soon as we reported the problem. I'm not saying our stay was horrible, but I think it's worth it to spend a few extra $$ and stay in a larger, more comfortable beachfront hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Neat little hotel We just returned from a stay at the Circle Hotel. It was only a 2 day stop from an inter Island flight to home. I wish it was a longer stay. The hotel has a very uncrowded feel while being in the best part of Waikiki. View units are definitely the way to go here as you can see the surfers, beachgoers, and special events on Kalakaua. It is a great base of operations for surfing during the summer and is close to the sights in the Waikiki area from the Zoo to the International Marketplace. I see a lot of bad comments about the small shower. It is small but plenty of room to shampoo and soap up...I wonder what other people use the shower for. I also notice that some people are not familiar with how to use a shower curtain.The room was very clean and big enough for what I do in Hawaii (which is not to spend all day inside). Service was just fine, no complaints at all. I will definitely go back, and next time, I'll bring friends.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great deal, perfect location! When my husband and I decided to stay at the Waikiki Circle this April, it was mainly for its convenient location (right across from the beautiful Waikiki beach, close to the International Market), but we got much, much more. First of all, the hotel didn't lie about the ocean view. The partial ocean-view room we booked offered an impressively expansive view. Second, I found the hotel very clean and the staff helpful (not artificially cheerful). Third, considering its location, this hotel is cost-friendly. Finally, the fastest elevator in town! Because this hotel is small, I never had to wait around for the elevater to arrive (like I did at other bigger and more expensive Waikiki hotels in the past). When you're back from the beach all wet, being able to catch the elevator right away is a GOOD thing. For those who are looking for a resort-type vacation, this hotel won't do. But I'd definitely stay at the Waikiki Circle again for its location, view, and value!

<Author>oliviasoma
<Content>Great stay!! Stayed in the Circle the first 5 days of June and it was great!! The clean rooms are small due to the circle shape of the hotel but the views from the 12th floor ocean front lanai are fantastic; Diamond Head to the east and Honolulu to the west. The staff was very friendly and helpful. Free use of beach towels, ice, personal items, downstairs phone, maps, and suggestions. Days of entertainment within walking distance. Beach across the street is gorgeous. Everyone is friendly and courteous. Plenty of places to eat both cheap and expensive. Your choice. Great street entertainment. Careful of the Ladies of the Night, they are aggressive. Go to the international market and barter for everything. They will practically pay you to take it!! Great bargains here. If you wait and purchase things to take home elsewhere, you will pay 3X the price. Ship things like coconuts and pineapples to loved ones. Great gift from Hawaii to find in your mailbox. Hope to stay at the Circle again! Aloha...sas

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Value, Wonderful View and Location We spent a week in Room 503 during May 2003 and could not have had a better time! It was the first trip to Hawaii for our 15 year old son.We paid extra for an oceanfront room, and were glad we did. On checking in, I requested a room no higher than the 6th floor so we could see all the action on the street. The staff was glad to grant my request. Since we paid a VERY low rate, we didn't expect a spectacular room (we don't go to Hawaii to stay in the room) but it was clean and comfortable enough for the 3 of us. The room was pretty small and the bathroom was tiny, but it had a big mirror and a nice-sized countertop to keep all our toiletries on. We also chose this hotel because it had an in-room refrigerator which allowed us to save money on breakfast and evening cocktails.Waking up to the spectacular view, having our Cheerios and orange juice, watching the waves, sipping Mai Tais and watching the sunset all from the private lanai was just priceless. My husband and son both surfed twice every day, and the hotel had a secure place on the ground level to store their boards which could be accessed anytime. If you go surfing, beware of the locals -- they don't mean well to the tourists. Otherwise it was a perfect vacation.I think the people who were unhappy with this hotel must have paid a lot higher room rate than we did, which might account for their higher expectations and comments that other hotels right on the beach were only a few dollars more. We booked through orbitz and didn't pay anywhere near $107 per night for our oceanfront room!We'd go back in a heartbeat if we hadn't purchased our own condo in Waikiki last month.

<Author>johnti006
<Content>Excellent Value We just got back from a stay at this hotel March 10-16 and couldn't be happier with our choice. This hotel is right in the center of the action. We got an Ocean View room which has an angled view of the beach. The balcony is huge  we would sit out in the early afternoon  watch the surfers. The location though is unbelievable. I would not stay anywhere else, with the exception of the Sheraton Moana ($245 a night). <Author>Tommy2pdx
<Content>You Shoulda Stayed There Before the Remodel Caveat emptor is usually the phrase of the day when staying at admittedly budget hotels which this used to be before it had a serious upgrade/remodel in 1996. I stayed at The Waikiki Circle Hotel twice a year (usually April and first two weeks of December) from 1982-1995. At the time the place was in some disrepair and sorely needed a facelift, as the Aston chain later gave it. The pro's and con's tilted squarely onto the pro side at that time due to a number of factors, the chief one being the obscenely low rates. In 1982 a high floor ocean view room was (brace yourself) $29.00 per night and at the end in 1995 around $65.00 a night. While in the US Army at Schofield Barracks (near Wahiawa) from 1976-'79, I discovered this little gem. The pro's were: directly across the street from Waikiki Beach; hotel parking ($2.00 per night in'82 and $8.00 in '95) and yes the slots are limited to about a dozen and are extremely narrow so rent the smallest subcompact you can if you intend to stay here; restaurants, stores, attractions close by; centrally located about midway down the island that is Waikiki (and on the prettier less trashy half); spacious lanais that afforded great people watching, sunsets and ocean views and finally did I mention how CHEAP it was? The con's were: air conditioners that were less than reliable (that's where being on a high floor helped due to ever present tradewinds); shabby decor: carpet that looked and felt similar to concrete; bathroom fixtures from the '40's; flimsy louvres near closet and sliding glass doors that rattled at night and finally, as all hotels and homes are wont to have in Hawaii, copius amounts of cockroaches. I can happily report however, after two subsequent stays (December 1997 and March 2002) that all of the pro's still endure (except the rates, of course, but the ocean view rooms are still about a third cheaper than other ocean view rooms along the beach) and that the con's have been eliminated with the remodel. We saw nary a cockroach on either stay but those parking slots are as miniscule as ever. Overall, bearing in mind that this property is over 50 years old, it is still asthetically pleasing, comfortable (perhaps crowded if more than 2 are in a room) and a relative bargain. I would recommend to anyone, except perhaps Donald Trump. Besides, you'll be out discovering the natural beauty of Hawaii and all that Aloha anyway!  
<Date>Jan 5, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic View!!!!!!!!!!!  The Waikiki Circle is my favorite place to stay! We sat on the Lanai for breakfast every morning and just took in the breathtaking view. The water is such a beautiful color!! We had a partial ocean view room, but if we walked out on to the lanai and turned toward the ocean, their was a fantastic, unobstructed view of the ocean and beach. We turned the chairs to face the beach with the little table in front of us with our breakfast on it. We could have stayed there all day! But there is so much to do on Oahu that we didn't spend much time in our room. The fact that the room wasn't large wasn't a problem. We don't go to Hawaii to sit around in our room. The room was clean and the bed spreads were particularly lovely. I will positively return!!!!
